  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_36b1c347-9a10-4a12-b49e-92ed86fc5bad'
      });
    }

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer1782489635002385716">My name is Avocet Abigail Jackson. But because Mama couldn't find anyone who thought Avocet was a fine name for a child, she called me Bird. Which is okay by me. She named both her children after birds, her logic being that if we were named for something with wings then maybe we'd be able to fly above the shit in our lives. . . .                      <br/><br/> So says Bird Jackson,</span>
  <span id="freeText1782489635002385716" style="display:none">My name is Avocet Abigail Jackson. But because Mama couldn't find anyone who thought Avocet was a fine name for a child, she called me Bird. Which is okay by me. She named both her children after birds, her logic being that if we were named for something with wings then maybe we'd be able to fly above the shit in our lives. . . .                      <br /><br /> So says Bird Jackson, the mesmerizing narrator of Connie May Fowler's vivid and brilliantly written, <b>Before Women Had Wings</b>.                       <br /><br />Starstruck by a dime-store picture of Jesus, Bird fancies herself "His girlfriend" and embarks upon a spiritual quest for salvation, even as the chaos of her home life plunges her into a stony silence. In stark and honest language, she tells the tragic life of her father, a sweet-talking wanna-be country music star, tracks her older sister's perilous journey into womanhood, and witnesses her mother make a courageous and ultimately devastating decision.                      <br /><br />Yet most profound is Bird's own story--her struggle to sift through the ashes of her parents' lives, her meeting with Miss Zora, a healer whose prayers over the bones of winged creatures are meant to guide their souls to heaven, and her will to make sense of a world where fear is more plentiful than hope, retribution more valued than love. . . .                     <br /><br />"A thing of heart-rending beauty, a moving exploration of love and loss, violence and grief, forgiveness and redemption."           <br />--<b>Chicago Tribune</b>                      <br /><br />"There is no denying the depth of Connie May Fowler's talent and the breadth of her imagination."           <br />--<b>The New York Times Book Review</b>                      <br /><br />"Brilliant."           <br />--<b>The Boston Sunday Globe</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="1782489635002385716" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/280959421" />
    <a title="Kate" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2703554-kate"><img alt="Kate" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1382111960p2/2703554.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/280959421?book_show_action=true">Feb 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kate" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kate" href="/user/show/2703554-kate">Kate</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer280959421" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5250635969739489426">This book should be depressing. It really should be, but when I read the final word and closed the book for the last time, I came away with an awesome sense of hope. Connie May Fowler expertly explores themes of growing up, poverty, abuse, abandonment and grief. The graphic descriptions of abuse, both physical and verbal, turned my stomach, but rather than being voyeuristic, the pain enhanced the feeling of hope. Readers actually believed that the characters could break out of the spiral they fi</span>
  <span id="freeText5250635969739489426" style="display:none">This book should be depressing. It really should be, but when I read the final word and closed the book for the last time, I came away with an awesome sense of hope. Connie May Fowler expertly explores themes of growing up, poverty, abuse, abandonment and grief. The graphic descriptions of abuse, both physical and verbal, turned my stomach, but rather than being voyeuristic, the pain enhanced the feeling of hope. Readers actually believed that the characters could break out of the spiral they find themselves in. In fact most of the dramatic tension comes in the interplay between the hope and the disappointment. Fowler captures the voice of a young girl, masterfully, looking at the world through her eyes we explore it as a child would, see it as a child would and ask questions that a child would ask when living in a grown up world. Before Women Had Wings is both heart breaking and restoring. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5250635969739489426" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8599147712916519002">I LOVED this book! It takes place in the mid sixies in Florida and is narrated by a young girl who was the same age I was when I lived in Florida then. I could just breathe that humid, salty clime that was part and parcel of my childhood! But this book has a serious theme--the abuse, alcoholism, and poverty that children are victims to through no fault of their own. It is painful to visit such themes but the wonderful "grace-note" of a surprising savior to the protaganist, Bird (how southern a n</span>
  <span id="freeText8599147712916519002" style="display:none">I LOVED this book! It takes place in the mid sixies in Florida and is narrated by a young girl who was the same age I was when I lived in Florida then. I could just breathe that humid, salty clime that was part and parcel of my childhood! But this book has a serious theme--the abuse, alcoholism, and poverty that children are victims to through no fault of their own. It is painful to visit such themes but the wonderful "grace-note" of a surprising savior to the protaganist, Bird (how southern a name--I had a great Aunt Bird in my life...) I want all my girlfriends to read this book. I got my copy from the library.</span>

<div id="review_444396893" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/444396893" />
    <a title="Joanna Bastian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2614128-joanna-bastian"><img alt="Joanna Bastian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1267120718p2/2614128.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/444396893?book_show_action=true">Oct 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joanna Bastian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joanna Bastian" href="/user/show/2614128-joanna-bastian">Joanna Bastian</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer444396893" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10893138575390484416">"Details are what I'm about - stacks and stacks of details - the bones of my family, calcified vessels, the marrow chock-full of wishes and regrets. In my mind I pick up the bones one by one - a leg bone, a hip, then a spine that looks like a witch's ladder. Before you know it, this skeleton made of memories is rattling me." <br/>So begins the tale of a six year old girl in 1965 Florida. The tale is rich in details that convey the stifling humidity, the salty scents, and the ring of the cidadas. Avoc</span>
  <span id="freeText10893138575390484416" style="display:none">"Details are what I'm about - stacks and stacks of details - the bones of my family, calcified vessels, the marrow chock-full of wishes and regrets. In my mind I pick up the bones one by one - a leg bone, a hip, then a spine that looks like a witch's ladder. Before you know it, this skeleton made of memories is rattling me." <br />So begins the tale of a six year old girl in 1965 Florida. The tale is rich in details that convey the stifling humidity, the salty scents, and the ring of the cidadas. Avocet Abigal Jackson tells her story of finding her own wings while trying to be strong for a family that has lost it's bearings. The imagery is vivid, the writing captivating.<br />I loved loved loved this tale and couldn't put the book down. I found this book on an airline, in the seat pocket. There is a name and address on a slip of paper that fell into my lap when I reached page 143. I am considering one of two options:<br />A) Sending the book to that address along with a note of appreciation for letting me 'discover' it.<br />B) Leaving the book on another flight for someone else to discover it, and then sending a thank you note to the address I found in the book. <br />What would you do with a phenomenal book?</span>
  <a data-text-id="10893138575390484416" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText12623750578540534310" style="display:none">I had always wanted to read this book because Connie May Fowler was a member of the writing community where I lived in Central Florida from 2004-2006, and I saw her frequently at literary events, and I'd heard great things about this book. I finally decided that this was the summer off from teaching that I would read it, and I'm so pleased that I did.<br /><br />Connie May Fowler can create sympathy in dysfunctional characters in a way that few other writers can. I really enjoyed her portrayal of the young sisters Bird and Phoebe coping with their abusive parents and the fact that the parents were round, believable characters. I felt that the conclusion of the book was wrapped up a little too quickly, but it was a five-star read nonetheless.</span>

<div id="review_299530780" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/299530780" />
    <a title="Marci" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2158638-marci"><img alt="Marci" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/299530780?book_show_action=true">Mar 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marci" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marci" href="/user/show/2158638-marci">Marci</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer299530780" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer878312190163157380">I want to give this book 3.5 stars, perhaps 4. I really enjoyed this book beginning to end. I read it in basically two sittings, not wanting to put it down -the story was so riveting. I had a few problems with some of the writing and tone of the book and that is why I downgraded it to 3.5. <br/><br/>The two issues I had were that the character is 9 years old and has some very profound thoughts, which I found hard to believe came from a 9 year old. And, although it is clear during most of the story that it</span>
  <span id="freeText878312190163157380" style="display:none">I want to give this book 3.5 stars, perhaps 4. I really enjoyed this book beginning to end. I read it in basically two sittings, not wanting to put it down -the story was so riveting. I had a few problems with some of the writing and tone of the book and that is why I downgraded it to 3.5. <br /><br />The two issues I had were that the character is 9 years old and has some very profound thoughts, which I found hard to believe came from a 9 year old. And, although it is clear during most of the story that it is being told in past tense it is still confusing to decipher what thoughts she is having as a 9 year old and what it being reflected back onto the little girl from the narrator's later 'older self' perspective. The positive outcome of the more advanced perspective is that it is engaging to an adult reader even though the main character is a child. <br /><br />The other issue is that although most of the writing is fresh and original, this author does not shy away from cliches and in a few instances, overused cliches. <br /><br />With that said, I loved this book and highly recommend it. It can be therapeutic for those who have been in abusive situations, either abuser or abused. At times the subject matter is distressing but in context, can be healing. I would compare this book to others like, Glass Castle and White Oleander. If you liked those books you are pretty likely to like this one. </span>
  <a data-text-id="878312190163157380" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_39932504" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/39932504" />
    <a title="Ruby" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1167229-ruby"><img alt="Ruby" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1227490955p2/1167229.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/39932504?book_show_action=true">Dec 12, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ruby" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ruby" href="/user/show/1167229-ruby">Ruby</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1167229-ruby?shelf=novels">novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1167229-ruby?shelf=women-feminist">women-feminist</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer39932504" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11765988868203666782">(Autobiographical Novel)—"Back in 1965, on a day so hot that God Almighty should have been writhing with sick-to-the-stomach guilt over driving His children out of the cool green of Eden, my daddy walked into our general store, held a revolver to his head, told my mama that he couldn't take any more and that because of her harsh ways and his many sins he was going to blow his brains out." What an opening sentence! Totally gripping. It demands that you keep reading while deftly establishing the v</span>
  <span id="freeText11765988868203666782" style="display:none">(Autobiographical Novel)—"Back in 1965, on a day so hot that God Almighty should have been writhing with sick-to-the-stomach guilt over driving His children out of the cool green of Eden, my daddy walked into our general store, held a revolver to his head, told my mama that he couldn't take any more and that because of her harsh ways and his many sins he was going to blow his brains out." What an opening sentence! Totally gripping. It demands that you keep reading while deftly establishing the voice and tone of this autobiographical novel. Resolving this incident takes the first 15-20 pages and then the initial breakneck pace of the novel slows to consider the day-in-day-out bewilderment of a child growing up in an abusive family with parents who can't even navigate their own emotional landscapes, much less guide their children. The writing is superb but the story is painful. Knowing that Fowler was exorcising the ghosts of her own past helped me endure the pain through to the happy ending when the women in this family do finally sprout wings, amazingly through the loving kindness and maturity of a neighbor.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11765988868203666782" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4255614967054534056">I'm not a big fan of the cover. Between that black and white photo of a wooden cabin and the blurb I had the sense it would read like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/59091.Tobacco_Road__Brown_Thrasher_Books_' title='Tobacco Road (Brown Thrasher Books) by Erskine Caldwell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Tobacco Road</a>. So I had this feeling that it would read as if it were set in 1940, not 1960s and was startled when 60's items (orange juice can rollers, granny bags) were introduced. <br/><br/>Fowler is a fine writer...but you know, I don't think I'll be reading other novels from her. The abuse is just too violent (and perhaps described too well.) In the back I read that thi</span>
  <span id="freeText4255614967054534056" style="display:none">I'm not a big fan of the cover. Between that black and white photo of a wooden cabin and the blurb I had the sense it would read like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/59091.Tobacco_Road__Brown_Thrasher_Books_" title="Tobacco Road (Brown Thrasher Books) by Erskine Caldwell" rel="nofollow noopener">Tobacco Road</a>. So I had this feeling that it would read as if it were set in 1940, not 1960s and was startled when 60's items (orange juice can rollers, granny bags) were introduced. <br /><br />Fowler is a fine writer...but you know, I don't think I'll be reading other novels from her. The abuse is just too violent (and perhaps described too well.) In the back I read that this story is very close to her life which made it even sadder and me more depressed. <br /><br />Others said they felt this had a hopeful ending...but an ending chapter explaining how everything went would have been better. </span>

  <span id="freeText17412787150768421651" style="display:none">Birdie grew up the youngest of three children to a rough, tough, and rowdy world of parents who fought, drank and involved her in their family drama. With beatings and verbal abuse daily Bird try's to stay out of their way but rarely suceeds. Every day her father rhreatens to kill himself in front of Bird and he finally succeeds. Bird is led to believe by her mother's words that its all her fault. Its funny the things children believe. <br /><br />When her mother moves the family to Florida into a decerped, derelict motel with individual units she meets her savior. Miss. Zora is Birds life line and although Bird's mother tries her best to sabotage the relationship out of spite jealousy, and fear, it flourishes. <br /><br />Bird's sensitive, tender heart and body takes quite a battering following her fathers death but Ms. Zora, and Bird's older brother who flits in and out of her life help her to navigate. One night after a terrible beating 7 year old Bird runs away and she meets a biker that befriends her and shows her how to fly one dark night on the back of a motorcycle and forget her troubles. <br /><br /> Bird's ability to find joy in small things like a dove with glitter on it, a three legged dog named Sam, a Dr. Pepper, swimming at the motel pool, talks with Ms. Zora, and dreams of a red bicycle with a banana seat help her survive. Fly Avocet, Fly sweet girl.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer263108818694076910">This book is a page turner, but towards the end it’s nerve racking to turn them because you’re afraid of what might happen! <br/>Bird is a sweet, innocent girl trying to grow up and learn what life is supposed to be about.   <span id="freeText263108818694076910" style="display:none">This book is a page turner, but towards the end it’s nerve racking to turn them because you’re afraid of what might happen! <br />Bird is a sweet, innocent girl trying to grow up and learn what life is supposed to be about. It’s sad how much violence she encounters yet she remains pretty hopeful overall. I wish her siblings could’ve done more to help her along the way. I knew Miss Zora would be an angel the minute they met. It was hard to believe her stubborn, drunk Mama would take Miss Zora’s advice so quickly - that was the only part of the story that didn’t seem realistic to me. Although, I did enjoy the ending very much, I had no idea where the story was going until then. </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1002049395" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5395108208739321578">This book is about domestic abuse between spouses and to children, drinking, hopelessness and poverty. Painful to read, very difficult to continue when expecting the next violent act, the next horrible name calling. In a way I can understand people acting and reacting in the cycle of violence passed from parents to children, but the action of Bird's father, taken when he was trying to punish his wife, was one of the most cold-blooded acts of domestic violence I have ever heard of. I didn't forgi</span>
  <span id="freeText5395108208739321578" style="display:none">This book is about domestic abuse between spouses and to children, drinking, hopelessness and poverty. Painful to read, very difficult to continue when expecting the next violent act, the next horrible name calling. In a way I can understand people acting and reacting in the cycle of violence passed from parents to children, but the action of Bird's father, taken when he was trying to punish his wife, was one of the most cold-blooded acts of domestic violence I have ever heard of. I didn't forgive him. <br />Two people outside of the family make the difference for Bird; Miss Zora - a great character (I want her in my own life), and the angel in guise of a big biker on a Harley outside a strip club. Within the family her big sister and big brother (although he is out of the house when much of the story occurs) are allies as they are all suffering through the same family violence, each trying to survive it in their own way.<br />This story, while fictional, is largely based on the events in Connie May Fowler's own violence filled upbringing.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5395108208739321578" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6573444006381790469">Avocet Abigail Jackson (aka Bird) is a character I won’t soon forget. Lots of brutal domestic violence and mental health issues could have made the book too full of despair, but Bird’s spirit of grit, forgiveness, strength, love, hope, and imagination overcomes the despair. Miss Zora is a life presence every child deserves. Luckily for many of us, Miss Zola is/was our mothers. <br/><br/>On a personal note... I finished this book yesterday. I was unable to sleep last night, and as I tossed and turned think</span>
  <span id="freeText6573444006381790469" style="display:none">Avocet Abigail Jackson (aka Bird) is a character I won’t soon forget. Lots of brutal domestic violence and mental health issues could have made the book too full of despair, but Bird’s spirit of grit, forgiveness, strength, love, hope, and imagination overcomes the despair. Miss Zora is a life presence every child deserves. Luckily for many of us, Miss Zola is/was our mothers. <br /><br />On a personal note... I finished this book yesterday. I was unable to sleep last night, and as I tossed and turned thinking about how Bird’s teacher, Mrs. Stepp, miserly failed Bird, my own students’ faces filled my mind and I prayed that I hadn’t failed any of them. <br /><br />Beautiful prose by the author. Here are a few examples:<br /><br />I kept my mouth shut, didn’t like the game - Mama playing Phoebe and me against each other. I was smart enough to know that there wouldn’t ever be any winners in a game based on mean-heartedness. (P 232)<br /><br />My mama is a good woman, full of bad deeds. (P 136)<br />My mama and daddy were not bad people, their mistakes were opportunities for me to practice forgiveness. (P 137)<br /><br />So I would gather my courage as if bravery and goodness were pebbles scattered all over the floor and I had to pick up those rocks of decency, one by one, and place them back in the sack of my soul. And when that sack was full, I would get out of bed and stumble in the darkness until I reached mama. (P 114)<br /><br />And there is this passage...<br /><br />I dug my nails into my wrists, and as the sting pushed back my tears, an awful notion struck me. It would be years before I could pin all the right words to the sickening feeling in the pit of my stomach, but this is what I felt: My family, we needed to get the hell out of this roach-infested shack stuck in the middle of the Devil’s grove. If we didn’t, we’d never be decent people with happy lives. No. We’d continue to be tiny chickens suffocating at the bottom of the heap. Bewildered folks - the sort moneyed people make fun of and never give jobs to. Dumb-assed crackers who drink till dawn in a sorry attempt to forget about all the things they will never have, never become. But there’s no forgetting when you’re white trash - smirks, stares, stolen glances remind you at every turn that you’re not worth squat. So the men, raging drunk, bullshit each other into believing that bruised fists and broken noses will act as charms, paving their way to heaven. And we females - girls and women alike - can’t find enough strength in our battered souls to escape, so we birth our boys into legendary scoundrels, characters made better in the crosshairs of half-truths. Yes, smiles break out all around as we cast daddies, brothers, husbands into near-respectable village idiots in stories we spin over bowls of home-grown, freshly snapped peas, clothslines draped with bleach-scented, bloodstained damp sheets, sinks filled with suds and supper-crusted dishes. And after that, we still aren’t decent. We’re still trapped. (Pp73-74)<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_82089432" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/82089432" />
    <a title="Krista" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2957439-krista"><img alt="Krista" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1518558802p2/2957439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/82089432?book_show_action=true">Oct 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Krista" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Krista" href="/user/show/2957439-krista">Krista</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer82089432" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13759604525211157803">It's hard to give a sad and slightly (more than slightly) disturbing book a high rating. It feels almost as if I'm in some way condoning or even endorsing those elements that made it an uncomfortable read from time to time. Of course, I'm not. I'm rating it on how much it made me feel and how well it was written. This is a book I would recommend to the right reader, but I would need to make sure that neglect, child abuse, and spousal abuse were not triggers for them. <br/><br/>Bird, our 8-year-old narrato</span>
  <span id="freeText13759604525211157803" style="display:none">It's hard to give a sad and slightly (more than slightly) disturbing book a high rating. It feels almost as if I'm in some way condoning or even endorsing those elements that made it an uncomfortable read from time to time. Of course, I'm not. I'm rating it on how much it made me feel and how well it was written. This is a book I would recommend to the right reader, but I would need to make sure that neglect, child abuse, and spousal abuse were not triggers for them. <br /><br />Bird, our 8-year-old narrator, is the youngest child of an abusive mother and mentally unstable father. Her parents' marriage is often turbulent and eventually results in bones that cannot be properly reset and a life that cannot be saved. When she ends up in Florida with what's left of her family, there is no relief. Poverty, alcoholism, neglect, and abuse continue to play major roles in her upbringing. Luckily, there is someone nearby who accepts and loves Bird for who she is. Miss Zora, a somewhat quirky and mysterious black woman who provides tea and wisdom whenever Bird needs them most, is the safe haven Bird needs when things are darkest in her world. <br /><br />There is a lot to consider when reading Bird's story, which is likely why there's a Book Club questionnaire appended to the story. Matters of alcoholism, abuse, poverty, and the role of women in society are just a few that immediately come to mind. So, if your book club is looking for a sober, literary read that can be unpackaged in a group setting, this might be something to consider.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13759604525211157803" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2115130029199410892">The character young "Bird" is caught in a despicable situation. An alcoholic father, who eventually kills himself, a physically and mentally abusive mother, and the worse part is, she knows nothing else and believes in her parents and this is love. I believe what I loved most about this story, are the saving graces and angels who come into her life and prove to her that love does not have to be so chaotic and hurtful and that there is some goodness. It is at the point in the story where, Bird ta</span>
  <span id="freeText2115130029199410892" style="display:none">The character young "Bird" is caught in a despicable situation. An alcoholic father, who eventually kills himself, a physically and mentally abusive mother, and the worse part is, she knows nothing else and believes in her parents and this is love. I believe what I loved most about this story, are the saving graces and angels who come into her life and prove to her that love does not have to be so chaotic and hurtful and that there is some goodness. It is at the point in the story where, Bird takes matters in her own hand and despite the constant negative claims she states to Bird about her friend, who is nothing but kind, she refuses to believe and eventually her mother changes. I liked the book, as I read it, it reminded within myself that often, people are raised and told certain situations are inevitable, it is all someone knows and if they are not touched by some other way, they may never know, life cannot be different. It is always good to read when and how a cycle is broken and a parent finally realizes they need help, but, unfortunately, this ending is not always as in this ending. But, I did enjoy the happy ending, it reminded me their are angels who enter people lives when even they do not know the difference. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1107841273898815274">I thought I'd offer a different perspective, I am a recovering alcoholic. As I was getting sober I started to realize the huge emotional abuse I inflicted on those around me. I wasn't a violent drunk but, would talk about hurting people and said a lot of cruel things and used fear to get my way.   <span id="freeText1107841273898815274" style="display:none">I thought I'd offer a different perspective, I am a recovering alcoholic. As I was getting sober I started to realize the huge emotional abuse I inflicted on those around me. I wasn't a violent drunk but, would talk about hurting people and said a lot of cruel things and used fear to get my way. I see myself as the character of the mother in this book, but the mother who comes back to her family after getting straight. My family has forgiven me but are still scarred by my behavior. As for me it's cost me jobs, friends, and caused me health problems not to mention the wasted years I spent drinking. Drinking is a huge problem in our country, but a lot of drunks are loving people who were hurt when they were younger and used booze to try and numb the pain. Booze turns drunks into monsters that nobody should have to put up with but can be redeemable if their strong enough to face their fears and quit drinking.</span>

<div id="review_2613282585" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2613282585" />
    <a title="Jill Caugherty" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/88600687-jill-caugherty"><img alt="Jill Caugherty" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581942464p2/88600687.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2613282585?book_show_action=true">Dec 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jill Caugherty" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jill Caugherty" href="/user/show/88600687-jill-caugherty">Jill Caugherty</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2613282585" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5733796718470857126">The narrative voice of Bird, the young protagonist of this amazing coming-of-age novel, strengthens after the first few chapters and quickly paints a deeply compelling, poignant, true-to-life portrait of a poor family's struggles. Bird grapples with her family's terrible poverty and circumstances, including the abuse she endures at the hands of her mother and the untimely suicide of her father. As she searches to understand her corner of the world and her place in it, she finds a type of salvati</span>
  <span id="freeText5733796718470857126" style="display:none">The narrative voice of Bird, the young protagonist of this amazing coming-of-age novel, strengthens after the first few chapters and quickly paints a deeply compelling, poignant, true-to-life portrait of a poor family's struggles. Bird grapples with her family's terrible poverty and circumstances, including the abuse she endures at the hands of her mother and the untimely suicide of her father. As she searches to understand her corner of the world and her place in it, she finds a type of salvation, healing, and meaning when an unlikely character, Zora, becomes a friend who listens to her and treats her with an importance she has never before known. Not only does Zora place balms on her physical wounds, she also ultimately attempts to heal emotional and psychological wounds, too, by helping Bird, her sister Phoebe, and their mother break the cycle of abuse and find a better way. Bird is a protagonist whose story will remain with me for a long time.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5733796718470857126" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer11367160160937737198">I picked this book up at a clearance sale without reading the synopsis or first few pages like usual. The title and cover intrigued me enough so I added it to my stack of new finds with thoughts of eventually getting to it. <br/><br/>Little did I know when I picked it up again to finally read it, I wouldn't be able to put it down. I read it in two sittings but could have easily gobbled it up in just one. I was engulfed in the story right from the start. The author does an amazing job or giving the right a</span>
  <span id="freeText11367160160937737198" style="display:none">I picked this book up at a clearance sale without reading the synopsis or first few pages like usual. The title and cover intrigued me enough so I added it to my stack of new finds with thoughts of eventually getting to it. <br /><br />Little did I know when I picked it up again to finally read it, I wouldn't be able to put it down. I read it in two sittings but could have easily gobbled it up in just one. I was engulfed in the story right from the start. The author does an amazing job or giving the right amount of details to make you feel like an invisible bystander but not bore you to death. She weaves together tales of pain, hope, despair and faith simultaneously in a way that feels very much like real life. <br /><br />This was my first read from this author but I'm not anxious to get my hands on some more of her work. </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('PE77daUr29lMyWMkdRt5XFdUjtkFNSU+9SkZyKqjQwvNi2Gfv4MLHil0VCriuMJTaijIW6v+ixZdqt9vHPJgAg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('nPw7El/n0cAt7cbiSz04lF9kiGLwOdqnKrUyUDR3YONtOaH4RU8BB0hQ8ezcnoObYhjO4F7ydI+CNvT3giZD6g==')})
  }

Since their mother died, Katie and her older sister, Diane, have struggled to understand their increasingly distant, often violent father. While Diane escapes into the arms of her boyfriend, Katie hides in her room or escapes to her best friend’s house—until Katie’s admiration for her strong-willed sister leads her on an adventure that transforms her life. Marvelously written, expertly told, The World Below captures the shadowy half-truths of the visible world, and the beauty and sorrow submerged beneath the surfaces of our lives--the lost world of the past, our lost hopes for the future. Abandoned by her mother as a child, mistreated by her father, and teased by her schoolmates (“Hey, Olive Oyl, where’s Popeye?”), the lonely girl finds solace in artistic pursuits. Only when she’s hired by the town’s sole feminist to work the night shift in the local thread factory does Violet come into her name, and bloom. Accepted by her co-workers, the teenager enters the happiest phase of her life, until a terrible accident causes her to retreat once again into her lonely shell.\n\nRealizing that she has only one clear choice, Violet boards a bus heading west to California. But when the bus crashes in North Dakota, it seems that fate is having another cruel laugh at Violet’s expense. This time though, Violet laughs back. She and her fellow passengers are rescued by two men: Austin Sykes, whom Violet is certain is the blackest man to ever set foot on the North Dakota prairie, and Kjel Hedstrom, who inspires feelings Violet never before has felt. Kjel and Austin are musicians whose sound is like no other, and with pluck, verve, and wit, Violet becomes part of their quest to make a new kind of music together. \n\nOh My Stars is Lorna Landvik’s most ambitious novel yet, with a cast of characters whose travails and triumphs you’ll long remember. It is a tale of love and hope, bigotry and betrayal, loss and discovery–as Violet, who’s always considered herself a minor character in her own life story, emerges as a heroine you’ll laugh with, cry
